=== URL: https://docs.ipfdev.co.uk/core/IPF_RELEASE_2024.3.0/iso20022-model/guides/migrating-from-legacy-model.html ===
Migrating from the legacy IPF Payment Model
IPF has a previous implementation of the ISO20022 Message model based on JAXB generation, and has an amount of core
components that leverage this and support this.
The initial introduction of the "new" message model is targeted and regression tested to provide exact like-for-like
representation of the messages. To this effect we observe the following principles
Principles
The JSON and XML representation of each Message Definition is identical between the old model and the new model,
as such API representations, and deserialisation from mongoDB as a nested property i.e. existing Domain Events do not
need any migration (A Domain Event persisted on the old model can be deserialised into the Domain Event that references
a ew model without any Json migration or other change needed).
Each model exists in a distinct maven artefact, and the classes are in distinct package structures, so both
representations can exist in a solution at runtime.
The new model also provides a migration-helper artifact that contains utility methods for converting between old and
new class representations (it does this by Json serialisation/deserialisation)
All core IPF components will only support the "new" model going forward, the old-model will not be provided as any
transitive dependency.
A solution is responsible for adopting the new model, adoption simply means a find-and-replace, replacing references
to message classes the old model with reference to the relevant classes in the new model. The relevant classes mappings
are documented here, but can also be found within the migration-helper utilities.
If a project does not want to migrate a particular usage of the old model, you will need manually add the dependency
to the old-model as part of the project dependencies, and then the migration-helper to convert an instances of the new
model message class to the equivalent old representation. This is not re-commanded as migration should be
straightforward - however this may be useful if the project has a custom component that persists instances of old class
versions.
New Message Model Artifact
The new message model can be found at the below artifact, it may be provided through transitive dependencies of core
components.
<dependency>
    <groupId>com.iconsolutions.iso20022.model</groupId>
    <artifactId>message-model</artifactId>
    <version>${icon-iso20022-model.version}</version>
</dependency>
This replaces the old model artifact, the below will no longer be pulled through as a dependency from core components
Old Model Artifact
<dependency>
    <groupId>com.iconsolutions.ipf.payments.domain</groupId>
    <artifactId>iso-domain-source</artifactId>
</dependency>
Auto-Migrating a project: OpenRewrite
To help with the migration of existing codebases we have provided an
OpenRewrite
recipe
that can be applied.
This recipe automatically updates the java references within a project that references old model classes to the
appropriate new model classes.
The recipe only updates Java references, and not any plaintext references (such as configuration files). It also does
not update any maven dependencies.
The maven dependencies will need to be manually updates as described above.
To run this on a downstream project, place the following maven plugin configuration in the root pom AND the
mps,domain,test,docs starter poms, since they do not inherit from the project parent and wonâ€™t inherit the config
otherwise
<build>
    <plugins>
        <plugin>
            <groupId>org.openrewrite.maven</groupId>
            <artifactId>rewrite-maven-plugin</artifactId>
            <version>4.38.0</version>
            <configuration>
                <activeRecipes>
                    <recipe>com.iconsolutions.iso20022.ISO20022MigrationRecipe</recipe>
                </activeRecipes>
            </configuration>
            <dependencies>
                <dependency>
                    <groupId>com.iconsolutions.iso20022</groupId>
                    <artifactId>iso20022-project-migrator</artifactId>
                    <version>1.1.2</version>
                </dependency>
            </dependencies>
        </plugin>
    </plugins>
</build>
Once the configuration has been added to the pom, execute the following steps in order:
Run the following command to convert java types from the old to the new types:
mvn org.openrewrite.maven:rewrite-maven-plugin:4.38.0:run
Manually update any non java reference, for example on config files
Add the
New Message Model Artifact
to the pom where needed if not brought in transitively.
Update the poms to the new release BOM version which contains the new data model
Run
mvn clean install
to confirm all is working and migrated
The plugin configuration does not need to remain within the project post migration and can be removed.
Migration Helper (Runtime Conversion)
If the old model classes are for some reason still require to exist on the downstream project, conversion between
instances of old model classes and new model classes can be performed by helper classes in the below see the below
supporting artifact
<dependency>
    <groupId>com.iconsolutions.iso20022.model</groupId>
    <artifactId>migration-pack</artifactId>
    <version>${icon-iso20022-model.version}</version>
</dependency>
See the utility methods within the MigrationHelper class, which provide methods to convert from instances of the old
model to the new model and visa-versa. This conversion is done through  the utility maintaining a mapping between the
legacy classes and the associated new model classes, providing lookup and conversion through serialisation and
de-serialisation via Json. It therefore incurs a small cost but allows full compatibility with any IPF components that
references the new data model classes (IPF APIs, Validations etc)
public class MigrationHelper {

    public static Object toOldModel(final Object anObject);

    public static <P> P toTargetClass(final Object anObject, Class<P> targetClass);
Type Maps
For completeness, we also provide the aforementioned underlying mappings between the old and new model class FQNs. These
aid with adoption of the new model for any references to classes that are not Java references, you can find the full
mappings, as tables, here:
